      • addBankAddr

        public void addBankAddr(java.lang.CharSequence param)
        Appends the specified BankAddr to the end of the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: Identifies the full name and address of a Beneficiary Bank, in respect of the Settlement Amount, where no Agent details are maintained for this Beneficiary Bank. This field provides flexibility during input of transactions where external movements of funds are involved. When you do not currently maintain a Customer reference for a third or fourth party bank, you can use this field to enter the full details of the name and address of the Beneficiary Bank directly. It is important to note that only one address, as free format, has been included in the module. This means that, in the case of a four party transfer, at least one of the two customers banks involved in the transfer of funds must have a Customer reference and the AGENCY defined. Once the payment has been sent, this field cannot be changed. for external delivery of Settlement Amount (Loss) -------------- -------------- | GLOBUS | | GLOBUS | | |=========>| NOSTRO | | BANK | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | -------------- -------------- | | | -------------- May be BEN.BANK1--------->| INTERMEDIARY | or BANK.ADDR--------->| | | | OPTIONAL | | | | | BANK | | | -------------- | | | -------------- May be BEN.BANK1--------->| ACCOUNT | or BEN.BANK2--------->| WITH | or BANK.ADDR--------->| | | | | | | BANK | | | -------------- MANDATORY IF PAYMENT THRU NOSTRO and no Agency details exist. The following summarises the rules concerning the use of the 3 fields BEN.BANK1, BEN.BANK2 and BANK.ADDR: (iv) BEN.BANK1 may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank(i.e. the final destination of the funds) or an INTERMEDIARY bank which will pass the funds onto a second bank. (v) BEN.BANK2 may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank (ie. the final destination of the funds) but may NOT be an INTERMEDIARY bank. (vi) BANK.ADDR may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank (i.e. the final destination of the funds) or it may be an INTERMEDIARY Bank which will pass the funds on to a second bank. It is only used if no customer ID is available. At contract loading, if the INTERMEDIARY Bank is identified in BEN.BANK1, then the ACCOUNT WITH Bank must be input either directly at BEN.BANK2 or within BANK.ADDR in which case the system will automatically apply it to BEN BANK2. Otherwise, when the INTERMEDIARY Bank is identified within BANK.ADDR - (and is thus automatically applied to BEN.BANK1) then the ACCOUNT WITH Bank must be identified in BEN.BANK2. Validation Rules: 1 to 4 lines of 35 Alpha-numeric characters. - Type AAA. Multi-value field. (Optional input when SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro and settlement amount is a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when the contract has been done at a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro. Input in this field will not be allowed if BEN.BANK1 and BEN.BANK2 have both been entered.

        Parameters:
        param - the BankAddr to append
        Returns:
        nothing

      • addBankAddr

        public void addBankAddr(TField param)
        Appends the specified BankAddr to the end of the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: Identifies the full name and address of a Beneficiary Bank, in respect of the Settlement Amount, where no Agent details are maintained for this Beneficiary Bank. This field provides flexibility during input of transactions where external movements of funds are involved. When you do not currently maintain a Customer reference for a third or fourth party bank, you can use this field to enter the full details of the name and address of the Beneficiary Bank directly. It is important to note that only one address, as free format, has been included in the module. This means that, in the case of a four party transfer, at least one of the two customers banks involved in the transfer of funds must have a Customer reference and the AGENCY defined. Once the payment has been sent, this field cannot be changed. for external delivery of Settlement Amount (Loss) -------------- -------------- | GLOBUS | | GLOBUS | | |=========>| NOSTRO | | BANK | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | -------------- -------------- | | | -------------- May be BEN.BANK1--------->| INTERMEDIARY | or BANK.ADDR--------->| | | | OPTIONAL | | | | | BANK | | | -------------- | | | -------------- May be BEN.BANK1--------->| ACCOUNT | or BEN.BANK2--------->| WITH | or BANK.ADDR--------->| | | | | | | BANK | | | -------------- MANDATORY IF PAYMENT THRU NOSTRO and no Agency details exist. The following summarises the rules concerning the use of the 3 fields BEN.BANK1, BEN.BANK2 and BANK.ADDR: (iv) BEN.BANK1 may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank(i.e. the final destination of the funds) or an INTERMEDIARY bank which will pass the funds onto a second bank. (v) BEN.BANK2 may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank (ie. the final destination of the funds) but may NOT be an INTERMEDIARY bank. (vi) BANK.ADDR may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank (i.e. the final destination of the funds) or it may be an INTERMEDIARY Bank which will pass the funds on to a second bank. It is only used if no customer ID is available. At contract loading, if the INTERMEDIARY Bank is identified in BEN.BANK1, then the ACCOUNT WITH Bank must be input either directly at BEN.BANK2 or within BANK.ADDR in which case the system will automatically apply it to BEN BANK2. Otherwise, when the INTERMEDIARY Bank is identified within BANK.ADDR - (and is thus automatically applied to BEN.BANK1) then the ACCOUNT WITH Bank must be identified in BEN.BANK2. Validation Rules: 1 to 4 lines of 35 Alpha-numeric characters. - Type AAA. Multi-value field. (Optional input when SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro and settlement amount is a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when the contract has been done at a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro. Input in this field will not be allowed if BEN.BANK1 and BEN.BANK2 have both been entered.

Validation Rules: Standard FRA ID i.e. FRYYDDDNNNNN Multivalue field. Standard ID Number in each expanded line. Input allowed in this field when POS OPEN/CLOSE = "Close". The FRA ID input in this field must be an existing and Live FRA contract and in the opposite sense of the current transaction (purchase <---> sale), open on the FRA Trading position file. This functionality is not available for contracts which has TR.DEAL.WISE.REVAL set to yes.

      • addConfNarrative

        public void addConfNarrative(TField param)
        Appends the specified ConfNarrative to the end of the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: To specify any narrative to be included on the confirmation sent to the counterparty. If the Floating Rate Option code defined in MARKET.RATE.TEXT is OTHER, which is mapped to the tag 14F of SWIFT confirmation, this field gets defaulted with the value from the field SWIFT.CODE.WORD followed by the value from the DESCRIPTION of the MARKET.RATE.TEXT. The SWIFT.CODE.WORD defined in MARKET.RATE.TEXT table is meant for use when the floating Rate Option code is OTHER. System, therefore, defaults the same if User has not keyed in the same word manually. As per SWIFT standards, the code FROP must be used if the Floating Rate Option code is OTHER. Therefore, a validation is provided to ensure that the FROP defaulted by system is retained and not manually deleted. MARKET.RATE.TEXT record is identified using REFERENCE.RATE key on the contract. In case a record is not found, then the MARKET.RATE.TEXT record that contains the RATE.KEY value same as the REFERENCE.RATE is retrieved. When REFERENCE.RATE KEY is found in multiple records,the first record of MARKET.RATE.TEXT is considered after sorting by ID. This field is mapped to the tag 72 of the SWAP Confirmation Message. Validation Rules: Multivalue field. 35 alphanumeric characters. Input is optional and no default is applicable. Maximum 4 lines of 35 characters.

        Parameters:
        param - the ConfNarrative to append
        Returns:
        nothing

      • addOverride

        public void addOverride(TField param)
        Appends the specified Override to the end of the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: Contains all the override messages which the user agreed to during input. During the validation stage of a FRA contract, the system may provide the user with a series of screen override messages to indicate an anomaly, for instance, that the interest rate varies by more thatn the variation tolerance defined in the FRA parameters table. In the event that the user confirms the Override, the full text of the actual Override Message will be stored, for reference purposes on in this multivalue field. For example, if the user inserts an 'abnormal' interest rate in the field corresponding to the interest rate then when the deal is validated a warning bell will sound and a message will appear, at the foot of the screen, which reads: 'VARIANCE OF RATE EXCEEDS PERMITTED TOLERANCE' This will draw the user's attention to the rate entered, which may be a mistake and can then be corrected, or, on the other hand, it may be correct input and so the user confirms that this rate is really intended. A second example might be in respect of a contract done with a client who has a credit line established with the bank but where the start date of the intended FRA contract goes beyond the credit line expiry date. In this case when the deal is validated a warning bell will sound and a message will appear, at the foot of the screen, which reads: 'LINE EXPIRES BEFORE TXN START DATE' Once again the user's attention is drawn to the situation and either corrected or conrimed via a positive response to the Override Message. If, subsequently, the contract record is either fully displayed or printed, then all override messages will be present. Validation Rules: Internal field. Multivalue field.

        Parameters:
        param - the Override to append
        Returns:
        nothing

      • addSetlAdvSent

        public void addSetlAdvSent(java.lang.CharSequence param)
        Appends the specified SetlAdvSent to the end of the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: Specifies the date and time when the settlement advice details have been passed over to the T24 Delivery module for onward communication to the receiver of the message. The FRA call to the T24 Delivery Module is acknowledged by the latter, sending back the ID it has generated for the message. This ID takes the following form: D 1986 1105 - 334335 where: D means a message is to be delivered (as opposed to R for a message received). 1986 is the current year 11 is the current month number 09 is the current day and, 334335 is a serial number taken form the computer time clock, i.e. the number of seconds (in tenths) elapsed since midnight. This number corresponds to 09:17:13 AM. Validation Rules: Content is automatically generated.

        Parameters:
        param - the SetlAdvSent to append
        Returns:
        nothing

      • addStmtNo

        public void addStmtNo(java.lang.CharSequence param)
        Appends the specified StmtNo to the end of the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: A sub-value number generated automatically by the system which identifies either a statement entry or a category entry in respect of a contract. The system will automatically insert a number into this field and this number may refer to a statement entry or a category entry depending on the value contained in the corresponding multivalue fields. The following examples will illustrate the use of this field. Example 1: On the start date of a FRA contract there will be an entry on the Settlement Account and the following type of number will be generated at this field: SV1 STMT.NO ........... 673732684.48 SV2 STMT.NO ........... 1 The number automatically generated in S.V.1 is unique to the contract in question and is built in the following way: 1. The first four digits '6737' indicate the number of days since the 1st of January 1968. In our example, it corresponds to the 11th of June 1986. 2. The next five digits '32684' indicate the number of seconds since midnight. In our example, it corresponds to an entry generated on line at 09:04:44 AM. 3. The last two digits '48' indicate the number of hundreds of seconds. The value assigned (again automatically) to S.V.2 identifies the number in S.V.1 as a statement entry number. If the user wishes to call this statement entry record on to the screen the user will invoke the STMT.ENTRY Application and then type the following at 'AWAITING ID': 67372684.480001 where the suffix '0001' identifies it as the first statement entry (there may be more than one as the next example will illustrate). Example 2: A second example outlined here is similar to example 1 in that there is a statement entry on start date for both the Settlement Account and the CHG/COM Acct. The system handles this case as follows: SV.1 STMT.NO ........... 673732684.48 SV.2 STMT.NO ........... 1-2 Once again S.V.1 contains the identification number automatically generated by the system while S.V.2 now contains two separate numbers signifying that there are in fact two separate statement entries, one in respect of the Settlement Account and one in respect of the CHG/COM Acct. If the user wishes to see either of these he must first of all invoke STMT.ENTRY followed by the desired function and then at 'AWAITING ID' type either: 673732684.480001 where the addition of the suffix '0001' identifies the statement entry in respect of the settlement account or, 673732684.480002 where the addition of the suffix '0002' identifies the statement entry in respect of the CHG/COM ACCT. Example 3: A third example might be that of a category entry generated at initiation of a contract where commission or charges have been debited to the customer and credited to a profit and loss category code. In this case the following entries are generated on the contract: SV1 STMT.NO ............... 673732684.48 SV3 STMT.NO ............... 1 Once again the standard type number is generated and inserted at S.V.1. Now, however, S.V.2 is replaced by S.V.3 which now identifies the number in S.V.1 as a category entry and not a statement entry. To call this category entry record onto the screen the user must now type: CATEG.ENTRY at 'AWAITING APPLICATION' followed by: 673732684.480001 at 'AWAITING ID' Validation Rules: Internal multivalue field.

        Parameters:
        param - the StmtNo to append
        Returns:
        nothing

      • clearBankAddr

        public void clearBankAddr()
        Clear the collection of BankAddr
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: Identifies the full name and address of a Beneficiary Bank, in respect of the Settlement Amount, where no Agent details are maintained for this Beneficiary Bank. This field provides flexibility during input of transactions where external movements of funds are involved. When you do not currently maintain a Customer reference for a third or fourth party bank, you can use this field to enter the full details of the name and address of the Beneficiary Bank directly. It is important to note that only one address, as free format, has been included in the module. This means that, in the case of a four party transfer, at least one of the two customers banks involved in the transfer of funds must have a Customer reference and the AGENCY defined. Once the payment has been sent, this field cannot be changed. for external delivery of Settlement Amount (Loss) -------------- -------------- | GLOBUS | | GLOBUS | | |=========>| NOSTRO | | BANK | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | -------------- -------------- | | | -------------- May be BEN.BANK1--------->| INTERMEDIARY | or BANK.ADDR--------->| | | | OPTIONAL | | | | | BANK | | | -------------- | | | -------------- May be BEN.BANK1--------->| ACCOUNT | or BEN.BANK2--------->| WITH | or BANK.ADDR--------->| | | | | | | BANK | | | -------------- MANDATORY IF PAYMENT THRU NOSTRO and no Agency details exist. The following summarises the rules concerning the use of the 3 fields BEN.BANK1, BEN.BANK2 and BANK.ADDR: (iv) BEN.BANK1 may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank(i.e. the final destination of the funds) or an INTERMEDIARY bank which will pass the funds onto a second bank. (v) BEN.BANK2 may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank (ie. the final destination of the funds) but may NOT be an INTERMEDIARY bank. (vi) BANK.ADDR may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank (i.e. the final destination of the funds) or it may be an INTERMEDIARY Bank which will pass the funds on to a second bank. It is only used if no customer ID is available. At contract loading, if the INTERMEDIARY Bank is identified in BEN.BANK1, then the ACCOUNT WITH Bank must be input either directly at BEN.BANK2 or within BANK.ADDR in which case the system will automatically apply it to BEN BANK2. Otherwise, when the INTERMEDIARY Bank is identified within BANK.ADDR - (and is thus automatically applied to BEN.BANK1) then the ACCOUNT WITH Bank must be identified in BEN.BANK2. Validation Rules: 1 to 4 lines of 35 Alpha-numeric characters. - Type AAA. Multi-value field. (Optional input when SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro and settlement amount is a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when the contract has been done at a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro. Input in this field will not be allowed if BEN.BANK1 and BEN.BANK2 have both been entered.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        nothing

      • clearConfNarrative

        public void clearConfNarrative()
        Clear the collection of ConfNarrative
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: To specify any narrative to be included on the confirmation sent to the counterparty. If the Floating Rate Option code defined in MARKET.RATE.TEXT is OTHER, which is mapped to the tag 14F of SWIFT confirmation, this field gets defaulted with the value from the field SWIFT.CODE.WORD followed by the value from the DESCRIPTION of the MARKET.RATE.TEXT. The SWIFT.CODE.WORD defined in MARKET.RATE.TEXT table is meant for use when the floating Rate Option code is OTHER. System, therefore, defaults the same if User has not keyed in the same word manually. As per SWIFT standards, the code FROP must be used if the Floating Rate Option code is OTHER. Therefore, a validation is provided to ensure that the FROP defaulted by system is retained and not manually deleted. MARKET.RATE.TEXT record is identified using REFERENCE.RATE key on the contract. In case a record is not found, then the MARKET.RATE.TEXT record that contains the RATE.KEY value same as the REFERENCE.RATE is retrieved. When REFERENCE.RATE KEY is found in multiple records,the first record of MARKET.RATE.TEXT is considered after sorting by ID. This field is mapped to the tag 72 of the SWAP Confirmation Message. Validation Rules: Multivalue field. 35 alphanumeric characters. Input is optional and no default is applicable. Maximum 4 lines of 35 characters.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        nothing

      • clearOverride

        public void clearOverride()
        Clear the collection of Override
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: Contains all the override messages which the user agreed to during input. During the validation stage of a FRA contract, the system may provide the user with a series of screen override messages to indicate an anomaly, for instance, that the interest rate varies by more thatn the variation tolerance defined in the FRA parameters table. In the event that the user confirms the Override, the full text of the actual Override Message will be stored, for reference purposes on in this multivalue field. For example, if the user inserts an 'abnormal' interest rate in the field corresponding to the interest rate then when the deal is validated a warning bell will sound and a message will appear, at the foot of the screen, which reads: 'VARIANCE OF RATE EXCEEDS PERMITTED TOLERANCE' This will draw the user's attention to the rate entered, which may be a mistake and can then be corrected, or, on the other hand, it may be correct input and so the user confirms that this rate is really intended. A second example might be in respect of a contract done with a client who has a credit line established with the bank but where the start date of the intended FRA contract goes beyond the credit line expiry date. In this case when the deal is validated a warning bell will sound and a message will appear, at the foot of the screen, which reads: 'LINE EXPIRES BEFORE TXN START DATE' Once again the user's attention is drawn to the situation and either corrected or conrimed via a positive response to the Override Message. If, subsequently, the contract record is either fully displayed or printed, then all override messages will be present. Validation Rules: Internal field. Multivalue field.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        nothing

      • clearSetlAdvSent

        public void clearSetlAdvSent()
        Clear the collection of SetlAdvSent
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: Specifies the date and time when the settlement advice details have been passed over to the T24 Delivery module for onward communication to the receiver of the message. The FRA call to the T24 Delivery Module is acknowledged by the latter, sending back the ID it has generated for the message. This ID takes the following form: D 1986 1105 - 334335 where: D means a message is to be delivered (as opposed to R for a message received). 1986 is the current year 11 is the current month number 09 is the current day and, 334335 is a serial number taken form the computer time clock, i.e. the number of seconds (in tenths) elapsed since midnight. This number corresponds to 09:17:13 AM. Validation Rules: Content is automatically generated.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        nothing

      • clearStmtNo

        public void clearStmtNo()
        Clear the collection of StmtNo
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: A sub-value number generated automatically by the system which identifies either a statement entry or a category entry in respect of a contract. The system will automatically insert a number into this field and this number may refer to a statement entry or a category entry depending on the value contained in the corresponding multivalue fields. The following examples will illustrate the use of this field. Example 1: On the start date of a FRA contract there will be an entry on the Settlement Account and the following type of number will be generated at this field: SV1 STMT.NO ........... 673732684.48 SV2 STMT.NO ........... 1 The number automatically generated in S.V.1 is unique to the contract in question and is built in the following way: 1. The first four digits '6737' indicate the number of days since the 1st of January 1968. In our example, it corresponds to the 11th of June 1986. 2. The next five digits '32684' indicate the number of seconds since midnight. In our example, it corresponds to an entry generated on line at 09:04:44 AM. 3. The last two digits '48' indicate the number of hundreds of seconds. The value assigned (again automatically) to S.V.2 identifies the number in S.V.1 as a statement entry number. If the user wishes to call this statement entry record on to the screen the user will invoke the STMT.ENTRY Application and then type the following at 'AWAITING ID': 67372684.480001 where the suffix '0001' identifies it as the first statement entry (there may be more than one as the next example will illustrate). Example 2: A second example outlined here is similar to example 1 in that there is a statement entry on start date for both the Settlement Account and the CHG/COM Acct. The system handles this case as follows: SV.1 STMT.NO ........... 673732684.48 SV.2 STMT.NO ........... 1-2 Once again S.V.1 contains the identification number automatically generated by the system while S.V.2 now contains two separate numbers signifying that there are in fact two separate statement entries, one in respect of the Settlement Account and one in respect of the CHG/COM Acct. If the user wishes to see either of these he must first of all invoke STMT.ENTRY followed by the desired function and then at 'AWAITING ID' type either: 673732684.480001 where the addition of the suffix '0001' identifies the statement entry in respect of the settlement account or, 673732684.480002 where the addition of the suffix '0002' identifies the statement entry in respect of the CHG/COM ACCT. Example 3: A third example might be that of a category entry generated at initiation of a contract where commission or charges have been debited to the customer and credited to a profit and loss category code. In this case the following entries are generated on the contract: SV1 STMT.NO ............... 673732684.48 SV3 STMT.NO ............... 1 Once again the standard type number is generated and inserted at S.V.1. Now, however, S.V.2 is replaced by S.V.3 which now identifies the number in S.V.1 as a category entry and not a statement entry. To call this category entry record onto the screen the user must now type: CATEG.ENTRY at 'AWAITING APPLICATION' followed by: 673732684.480001 at 'AWAITING ID' Validation Rules: Internal multivalue field.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        nothing

      • getAccrTodate

        public TField getAccrTodate()
        Returns the AccrTodate

        Field description: Indicates the Accrual Todate in the FRA currency, i.e. in the accrual currency. This amount will be updated by the End of day process on each accrual run. It must be remembered that for all HEDGE contracts, the settlement amount (profit or loss) which is received or paid on the settlement date will be accrued during the notional period of the FRA contract (from START to MATURITY date) as an interest income or expense. The offset to this entry is a contra entry in the suspense account "Unearned Interest and Discount" (when profit) or "Interest Paid In Advance" (when settlement amount = loss). Validation Rules: Standard T24 amount format. System generated field when the FRA.TYPE is equal to "HEDGE".

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The AccrTodate

      • getAccrualCcy

        public TField getAccrualCcy()
        Returns the AccrualCcy

        Field description: Indicates the currency in which the accrual amount will be done. This will always be in the currency of the contract. When this is a foreign currency, the exchange position will be updated on a daily basis by this amount. The equivalent in local currency will then be the entry in the profit and loss category which is calculated everyday using the prevailing middle rate. Validation Rules: System generated field. Access not allowed. Same as FRA CURRENCY.

        Parameters:

      • getActionType

        public TField getActionType()
        Returns the ActionType

        Field description: Part of Regulatory Reporting information to a Trade Repository. Under the Regulatory Reporting to a Trade Repository, it is not only the initial trade that is reported but also the life cycle events of the Trade that follow. A change in the action type is indicative of an event on the contract and requires to be reported. Change in Action Types is allowed both manually and automatically. Specifies the ACTION.TYPE that is populated based on the event on trade Input to this field is allowed only when OC module is installed Validation Rules: Allowed optional values are N, M, E, C, Z, O, R and P N denotes that the ACTION.TYPE is NEW. Value of 'N' is defaulted for a new contract. User is also allowed to change the status to N if the previous status is E. E denotes that the ACTION.TYPE is REVERSE or Correction. In case of wrongly entered UTI values or a Temporary UTI was used previously, the old UTI should be reported with ACTION.TYPE as 'E' for error reporting first and then change the Action Type to NEW after keying in the actual UTI. This way the previous reporting with temporary UTI is replaced by the one with final UTI. Action Type E is also used to undo the reporting of a particular transaction done which should not have been done reported at all in the first instance. M denotes that the ACTION.TYPE is MODIFIED. In case of change in the RATE.FIXING.DATE the ACTION.TYPE is set to 'M' C denotes that the ACTION.TYPE is CANCELLED. In case of any change in maturity/value date i.e. early termination of the contract should be reported with C. In FRA this MATURITY.DATE field is No change field. So ACTION.TYPE never gets populated automatically with type as C but It can be manually updated as c and the contract can be cancelled. Z denotes Compression update. This means the trade being reported is generated out of a compression activity. O denotes OTHER types. When OTHER is used, additional information as to what OTHER mean should be mentioned separately.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The ActionType

Otherwise, when the INTERMEDIARY Bank is identified within BANK.ADDR - (and is thus automatically applied to BEN.BANK1) then the ACCOUNT WITH Bank must be identified in BEN.BANK2. Validation Rules: 1 to 4 lines of 35 Alpha-numeric characters. - Type AAA. Multi-value field. (Optional input when SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro and settlement amount is a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when the contract has been done at a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro. Input in this field will not be allowed if BEN.BANK1 and BEN.BANK2 have both been entered.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        List<TField> -

      • getBenAcctNo

        public TField getBenAcctNo()
        Returns the BenAcctNo

        Field description: Identifies the Account details (number or name) of the Beneficiary (with his bank) to be credited, with the Settlement Amount (only allowed when contract has been done at a loss). This field concerns third party transfers where the customer is requesting an external delivery of the settlement amount and for which you have received Account Details corresponding to the final Beneficiary account. Any amendment to this field after payment has been sent will be refused. Validation Rules: 1 to 35 Characters - Type SSS. Multi-value field (Maximum of four lines). (Optional input when SETTLEMENT ACCT is a Nostro account; Default value = counterpart (i.e. CUSTOMER.ID) himself. Input in this field will only be allowed for transactions done at a loss and when the SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro account.

      • getBenBank1

        public TField getBenBank1()
        Returns the BenBank1

        Field description: Identifies the counterparty Bank where the payment of the Settlement Amount (loss) has to be done. This field is used when the counterparty does not require the funds to be credited to his current account but instead requests an external delivery of the funds to a Bank different to the one where you maintain your Nostro account. If this Bank does not yet exist on the Database, the user may: a) Create a new record in the CUSTOMER and AGENCY file which will contain the information necessary to generate automatically advices, confirmations etc. for this bank or, b) Use the Bank ADDRESS to directly input the name and address of the Counterparty Bank without having to create a Customer and/or an Agent record. This option is very useful if the settlement amount has to be paid to a bank which is rarely dealt with. As this field indicates the disposal of the settlement amount, it may only be used for contracts done at a loss for the Bank. Once the payment has been sent, this field can no more be changed. Validation Rules: 3-10 Character Mnemonic (Uppercase alpha, numeric or ".") - Type MNE. Input will be checked against the AGENCY file. or 1-6 Numeric character Agent code (Optional input when Settlement Account is a Nostro and Settlement amount is a loss). Input is only allowed when the contract has been done at a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when Settlement Account is a Nostro. Input in this field must correspond to a valid Agent on the AGENCY file. When use in conjunction with the BEN.BANK2 field, the two Customer references must differ. Input in this field will not be allowed at the same time with an input in BEN.BANK2 and BANK.ADDR.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The BenBank1

      • getBenBank2

        public TField getBenBank2()
        Returns the BenBank2

        Field description: Contains the Counterparty reference for the second Beneficiary Bank for the Settlement Amount. Used where contracts involve four party transfers of funds. If for example, at the start date of a FRA, the customer requests the delivery of the settlement amount to his account that he maintains with American Bank A, Detroit which has an account with American Bank B, New York, the User will then make the following input: (i) Default (or Enter) the standard Nostro account number in the SETTLEMENT.ACCT. This field is always used to indicate the account where the book-keeping entries must be recorded by the system. (ii) Enter the Agent code (Customer number) of the American Bank B, New York, in BEN.BANK.1. In case this Bank does not exist on the Database, the User can then enter the name and address of this Bank in BANK.ADDR. (iii) Enter the Agent code (Customer number) of the Bank of Detroit in this field. In case this Bank does not exist on the Database but there was a Customer reference for the Bank identified in the previous field, the User can enter the name and address of this Bank in BANK.ADDR. This means that at least one of the two banks must have been defined on the CUSTOMER and AGENCY files. (iv) Enter the beneficiary account number in BENEF.ACCT. Once the payment has been sent, this field can no more be changed. Validation Rules: 3-10 Character Mnemonic (Uppercase alpha, numeric or ".") Type MNE. Input will be checked against the AGENCY file. or 1-6 Numeric character Agent code. (Optional input when SETTLEMENT is a Nostro and settlement amount is a loss). Input is only allowed when the contract has been done at a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro. Input in this field must correspond to a valid Agent on the AGENCY file. When used in conjunction with BEN.BANK.1, the two customer references must differ. Input in this field will not be allowed if BEN.BANK.1 and BANK.ADDR have both been entered. The customer reference input must be different from the Customer reference of the Nostro account used in SETTLEMENT.ACCT.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The BenBank2

If no input is made a default will be calculated from the brokerage using the current mid market exchange rates. If the brokerage is specified in the same currency as the broker currency then the brokerage will be copied to this field. Validation Rules: Standard amount format for currency. (Optional Input. Input not allowed in this field if no BROKERAGE, or BROKERAGE.CCY has been specified. The amount must be in a valid format for the brokerage currency.       • getConfAdvSent

        public TField getConfAdvSent()
        Returns the ConfAdvSent

        Field description: Specifies the date and time when the confirmation details have been passed over to the T24 Delivery module for onward communication to the receiver of the message. The FRA call to the T24 Delivery Module is acknowledged by the latter, sending back the ID it has generated for the message. This ID takes the following form: D 1986 1105 - 334335 where: D means a message is to be delivered (as opposed to R for a message received). 1986 is the current year 11 is the current month number 09 is the current day and, 334335 is a serial number taken form the computer time clock, i.e. the number of seconds (in tenths) elapsed since midnight. This number corresponds to 09:17:13 AM. Validation Rules: Content is automatically generated.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The ConfAdvSent

      • getConfNarrative

        public TField getConfNarrative(int idx)
        Returns the ConfNarrative at the specified position in this collection.

        Field description: To specify any narrative to be included on the confirmation sent to the counterparty. If the Floating Rate Option code defined in MARKET.RATE.TEXT is OTHER, which is mapped to the tag 14F of SWIFT confirmation, this field gets defaulted with the value from the field SWIFT.CODE.WORD followed by the value from the DESCRIPTION of the MARKET.RATE.TEXT. The SWIFT.CODE.WORD defined in MARKET.RATE.TEXT table is meant for use when the floating Rate Option code is OTHER. System, therefore, defaults the same if User has not keyed in the same word manually. As per SWIFT standards, the code FROP must be used if the Floating Rate Option code is OTHER. Therefore, a validation is provided to ensure that the FROP defaulted by system is retained and not manually deleted. MARKET.RATE.TEXT record is identified using REFERENCE.RATE key on the contract. In case a record is not found, then the MARKET.RATE.TEXT record that contains the RATE.KEY value same as the REFERENCE.RATE is retrieved. When REFERENCE.RATE KEY is found in multiple records,the first record of MARKET.RATE.TEXT is considered after sorting by ID. This field is mapped to the tag 72 of the SWAP Confirmation Message. Validation Rules: Multivalue field. 35 alphanumeric characters. Input is optional and no default is applicable. Maximum 4 lines of 35 characters.

        Parameters:
        idx - idx of the element to return
        Returns:
        TField -

      • getDailyAccrual

        public TField getDailyAccrual()
        Returns the DailyAccrual

        Field description: Indicates the Daily accrual amount in the FRA (accrual) currency. This amount corresponds to the settlement amount divided by the number of calendar days in the notional period of the FRA contract. It must be remembered that for all HEDGE contracts, the settlement amount (profit or loss) which is received or paid on the settlement date will be accrued during the notional period of the FRA contract (from START to MATURITY date) as an interest income or expense. The offset to this entry is a contra entry in the suspense account "Unearned interest and discount" (when profit) or "Interest paid in advance" (when settlement amount = loss). Validation Rules: Standard T24 amount format. System generated field when the FRA TYPE is equal to "HEDGE".

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The DailyAccrual

      • getFraPeriod

        public TField getFraPeriod()
        Returns the FraPeriod

        Field description: Indicates which period is covered by the FRA contract. For example, a "6-9" called a "six against nine" agreement means that the bank wants to enter into an FRA for 3 months commencing 6 months after signing. Examples: "1-6" = 1 against 6 agreement "6-12" = 6 against 12 agreement "12-18" = 12 against 18 agreement Validation Rules: "nn-NN" where : nn = 1 to 99 NN = 1 to 99 NN > nn This field is optional and input is used to calculate automatically the "START" and "MATURITY" dates of the contract.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The FraPeriod

      • getFraType

        public TField getFraType()
        Returns the FraType

        Field description: Specifies the underlying strategy of the FRA transaction. Two main types exist: HEDGE <--------> TRADING A distinction is made between the two in order to allow different accounting procedures to be implemented and for the timing of the recognition of profits and losses and as to when they are to be incorporated into the balance sheet. HEDGE Transactions Because the maturity dates of deposits and other sources of funds available in the market do not always sufficiently match the maturity of banks' assets, bankers make use of interest rate hedging instruments to reduce their interest gap exposure to acceptable limits. The FRAs have become today a popular alternative to Financial Futures as a means of hedging interest rate exposure. In order for a bank to enter into a FRA for hedging purposes, the following conditions will apply: 1. The bank must have net assets or liabilities which are subject to interest rate risk. This condition must exist after commitments and anticipated transactions reducing the risk have been taken into account. 2. The FRA transaction must be designated as a hedge and must reduce the interest rate risk on exposed assets and liabilities. As it can be seen, a conscious decision is done at deal level and since FRAs may be tailored into individual requirements, it is easier for such a trade to qualify as a hedge than for normal exchange governed Financial Futures. TRADING Transactions Apart from Hedging facilities, bankers will operate for other purposes such as general trading and arbitrage. Since such activities may be deemed to be of a more speculative nature, the concept of revaluing such positions is of importance. In order to allow the segregation of the above trade concepts, the input of trades requires the inclusion of the type of trade. This will allow the system to distinguish trades into their relevant categories both for accounting purposes and for revaluing. Validation Rules: H(edge), T(rading). Default none; Input is always mandatory.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The FraType

      • getFttCollCptyTax

        public TField getFttCollCptyTax()
        Returns the FttCollCptyTax

        Field description: Provides the option to T24 bank to collect the Financial Transaction Tax payable by the Counterparty also. If yes, accounting entries are raised to collect counterpartys tax wherein customer Account is debited and Tax suspense Account is credited. The values No or Null means T24 bank does not collect the FTT payable by the counterparty or in other words the counterparty himself remits the FTT. This option is provided on the premise that where the counterparty is a customer of the bank ( not an interbank counterparty) the T24 bank assumes responsibility to collect and pay the FTT payable by the customer Validation Rules: Values allowed are Yes, No or Null. Default value will be from FRA.PARAMETER but can be overridden by the User.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The FttCollCptyTax

      • getInterestRate

        public TField getInterestRate()
        Returns the InterestRate

        Field description: Specifies the future fixed interest rate on the notional Deposit/ Placement. This rate is guaranteed and set at the time of the FRA transaction. On the RATE FIXING DATE, the prevailing interest rate for the period of the deposit/placement is determined and compared to this rate. Any difference between these rates is settled between the counterparties based on the nominal amount of the notional deposit/placement. Validation Rules: Any value is accepted. Input in this field is mandatory. Only a fixed interest rate type is accepted for FRA transactions. Floating or periodic interest rates are not allowed. The rate input will be checked against the PERIODIC.INTEREST rate table (for a similar current period in the same currency and for the same reference rate). Any variation greater than the one specified in the FRA.PARAMETER table will require an override.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The InterestRate

      • getMaturityDate

        public TField getMaturityDate()
        Returns the MaturityDate

        Field description: Specifies the maturity (ending) date of the FRA contract. When the FRA PERIOD has been entered, the maturity date will be calculated automatically by the system in the following way : it will take the calculated contract START.DATE and add the difference in number of months resulting from input in field FRA PERIOD. The result (after checking of the relevant HOLIDAY record) will be the Maturity date of the FRA. The following input is also allowed : "NNM" where NN = 01 to 99 M = Month indicator the number of months input is then added to the START.DATE to calculate the maturity date. Validation Rules: Standard date format. The date must be greater than the Start date. Any non working day will require an override. Any input will override the default calculation. Input in this field is mandatory if a FRA PERIOD was not defined previouly in the transaction.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The MaturityDate

      • getOcClgStatus

        public TField getOcClgStatus()
        Returns the OcClgStatus

        Field description: Part of Regulatory Reporting information to a Trade Repository. Denotes the OC Clearing Status. Input to this field is allowed only when OC module is installed Validation Rules: Allowed optional values are Bilateral, Submitted, Accepted, Rejected, Cleared and Terminated. BILATERAL - when a fresh contract is inputted this field should be updated as BILATERAL SUBMITTED - when the inputted contract is submitted to Trade Repository it should get updated as SUBMITTED.The previous clearing status of the contract should be BILATERAL when OC.CLG.STATUS of the contract is SUBMITTED both CLG.MEM.ID and CENTRAl.CLG.PARTY fields cannot be NULL ACCEPTED - when the contract is accepted by the Trade Repository it should get updated as ACCEPTED.The previous status should be SUBMITTED REJECTED - when the contract is rejected by the Trade Repository it should get updated as REJECTED.The previous status should be SUBMITTED CLEARED - When the status of the contract is ACCEPTED, User is expected to reverse the contract and enter a new one with Trade status as CLEAREDwhen the status is CLEARED fields like CENTRAL.CLG.PARTY, CLG.MEM.ID, BILATERAL.REF are mandatory Terminated - A cleared contract when cancelled/terminated by the Trade Repository should be updated as TERMINATED.The previous status should be CLEARED This is a no change field

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The OcClgStatus

      • getOverride

        public List<TField> getOverride()
        Returns the collection of Override

        Field description: Contains all the override messages which the user agreed to during input. During the validation stage of a FRA contract, the system may provide the user with a series of screen override messages to indicate an anomaly, for instance, that the interest rate varies by more thatn the variation tolerance defined in the FRA parameters table. In the event that the user confirms the Override, the full text of the actual Override Message will be stored, for reference purposes on in this multivalue field. For example, if the user inserts an 'abnormal' interest rate in the field corresponding to the interest rate then when the deal is validated a warning bell will sound and a message will appear, at the foot of the screen, which reads: 'VARIANCE OF RATE EXCEEDS PERMITTED TOLERANCE' This will draw the user's attention to the rate entered, which may be a mistake and can then be corrected, or, on the other hand, it may be correct input and so the user confirms that this rate is really intended. A second example might be in respect of a contract done with a client who has a credit line established with the bank but where the start date of the intended FRA contract goes beyond the credit line expiry date. In this case when the deal is validated a warning bell will sound and a message will appear, at the foot of the screen, which reads: 'LINE EXPIRES BEFORE TXN START DATE' Once again the user's attention is drawn to the situation and either corrected or conrimed via a positive response to the Override Message. If, subsequently, the contract record is either fully displayed or printed, then all override messages will be present. Validation Rules: Internal field. Multivalue field.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        List<TField> -

      • getPaySettlementAct

        public TField getPaySettlementAct()
        Returns the PaySettlementAct

        Field description: Identifies the account through which the settlement loss amount is to be settled. At initiation both settlement accounts (Receive and Pay) will be allowed in order to enable the correct generation of the SWIFT confirmation advice. When the settlement rate is entered later, the user will be requested to erase one of the two accounts depending on the profit/loss resulting from the settlement rate. When no input has been entered in this field, the system will proceed as follows: a) In a first stage, the application will check if the counterparty has specific instructions defined on the Agency table for the settlement currency. If yes, the existing conditions will be followed. Otherwise, b) In a second stage, the FRA application will check in the internal file Customer Ccy Acct if the counterparty with whom the bank is making the deal has an account in that currency (i.e. settlement currency). If yes, this customer account will then be credited. If the counterparty does not maintain an account in the settlement currency with the bank, c) The FRA application will then, in a third stage, find in the table NOSTRO ACCOUNT the relevant nostro account for the settlement currency. If this account exists on the Nostro table, it will then be used to record the credit accounting entry. If at the Nostro table more than one nostro exists per currency, the system will default to the first account listed. However, the user has the ability to select which Nostro account by entering 'A' to give the first, 'B' to give the second and so forth. If no account is defined on the Nostro table, d) The user will then need to enter an account number which can be a customer account, a nostro account or an internal account. The internal account details must be present on the FX.TEXT table. Input to this field for internal accounts must be entered in the format 1 to give the first account: 2 to give the second and so forth as detailed on the FX.TEXT table. Validation Rules: Standard Account number or Mnemonic. Default = As indicated here below. If entered as an account number or mnemonic, the account must be present on the accounts file and must be in the appropriate currency. An override is required where the account is not an account of the counterparty unless a nostro is specified. Posting restrictions require an override.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The PaySettlementAct

      • getPaymentSent

        public TField getPaymentSent()
        Returns the PaymentSent

        Field description: Specifies the date and time when the payment settlement details have been passed over to the T24 Delivery module for onward communication to the receiver of the message. This is only applicable when the contract is done at a loss. The FRA call to the T24 Delivery Module is acknowledged by the latter, sending back the ID it has generated for the message. This ID takes the following form: D 1986 1105 - 334335 where: D means a message is to be delivered (as opposed to R for a message received). 1986 is the current year 11 is the current month number 09 is the current day and, 334335 is a serial number taken form the computer time clock, i.e. the number of seconds (in tenths) elapsed since midnight. This number corresponds to 09:17:13 AM. Validation Rules: Content is automatically generated.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The PaymentSent

      • getPositionOpnClose

        public TField getPositionOpnClose()
        Returns the PositionOpnClose

        Field description: For the contracts which are specified as NON HEDGE, this will specify if the contract being done is to open (create) a new FRA position or to close an existing open FRA position. This information is important because a different accounting treatment exists for FRA positions which have been matched (closed) vis-a-vis the positions which are still unmatched (open). Validation Rules: Nil (when HEDGE contracts) Open (for TRADING contracts) Close (for TRADING contracts) Automatically defaulted by the system. "Open" or "Close" are mandatory for TRADING contracts. "Close" is only allowed if a position already exists on the dates (START.DATE and MATURITY.DATE) specified in the deal. "Open" will only be allowed for new or increases in existing positions. "Nil" is mandatory for HEDGE deals. This functionality is not available for contracts which has TR.DEAL.WISE.REVAL set to yes.

      • getSettlementAmt

        public TField getSettlementAmt()
        Returns the SettlementAmt

        Field description: Indicates the value of the amount to be settled. On the RATE.FIX.DATE of the FRA agreement, the fixed rate of the contract is compared with the settlement rate and counterparties settle between them the value of the interest rate differential on the agreed principal over the agreed period. Since the interest rate differencial is paid in advance at the START.DATE of the fixed rate period, the settlement amount is DISCOUNTED as per formula indicated in addendum. Thus, the settlement amount of a FRA is the profit or loss that is realised upon the settlement (START) date, and whose value is discounted back from the date of maturity. 1. When the SETTLEMENT.RATE is greater than the INTEREST.RATE of the FRA contract then: - If the FRA contract is an Asset (SALE), then the settlement amount is a LOSS and the settlement amount will be displayed with a "-" (minus) sign. - If the FRA contract is a Liability (PURCHASE), then the settlement amount is a PROFIT and the settlement amount will be displayed with a "+" (positive) sign. 2. When the SETTLEMENT.RATE is smaller than the INTEREST.RATE of the FRA contract then: - If the FRA contract is an Asset (SALE), then the settlement amount is a PROFIT and the settlement amount will be displayed with a "+" (positive) sign. - If the FRA contract is a Liability (PURCHASE), then the settlement amount is a LOSS and the settlement amount will be displayed with a "-" (minus) sign. Validation Rules: Standard amount format. System generated field. Access not allowed. Amount is always displayed in the currency of SETTLEMENT.CCY.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The SettlementAmt

      • getStartDate

        public TField getStartDate()
        Returns the StartDate

        Field description: Specifies the commencing (starting) date of the FRA contract. When the FRA PERIOD has been entered, the start date will be calculated automatically by the system in the following way : it will take the calculated market SPOT.DATE and add the number of months specified in the first part of the field FRA.PERIOD. The result (after checking of the relevant HOLIDAY record) will be the Start date of the FRA. The following input is also allowed : "NNM" where NN = 01 to 99 M = Month indicator the number of months input is then added to the SPOT.DATE to calculate the START.DATE. Validation Rules: Standard date format. The date must be greater than the Spot date. Any non working day will require an override. Any input will override the default calculation. Input in this field is mandatory if a FRA.PERIOD was not defined previously in the transaction.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The StartDate

      • getStmtNo

        public List<TField> getStmtNo()
        Returns the collection of StmtNo

        Field description: A sub-value number generated automatically by the system which identifies either a statement entry or a category entry in respect of a contract. The system will automatically insert a number into this field and this number may refer to a statement entry or a category entry depending on the value contained in the corresponding multivalue fields. The following examples will illustrate the use of this field. Example 1: On the start date of a FRA contract there will be an entry on the Settlement Account and the following type of number will be generated at this field: SV1 STMT.NO ........... 673732684.48 SV2 STMT.NO ........... 1 The number automatically generated in S.V.1 is unique to the contract in question and is built in the following way: 1. The first four digits '6737' indicate the number of days since the 1st of January 1968. In our example, it corresponds to the 11th of June 1986. 2. The next five digits '32684' indicate the number of seconds since midnight. In our example, it corresponds to an entry generated on line at 09:04:44 AM. 3. The last two digits '48' indicate the number of hundreds of seconds. The value assigned (again automatically) to S.V.2 identifies the number in S.V.1 as a statement entry number. If the user wishes to call this statement entry record on to the screen the user will invoke the STMT.ENTRY Application and then type the following at 'AWAITING ID': 67372684.480001 where the suffix '0001' identifies it as the first statement entry (there may be more than one as the next example will illustrate). Example 2: A second example outlined here is similar to example 1 in that there is a statement entry on start date for both the Settlement Account and the CHG/COM Acct. The system handles this case as follows: SV.1 STMT.NO ........... 673732684.48 SV.2 STMT.NO ........... 1-2 Once again S.V.1 contains the identification number automatically generated by the system while S.V.2 now contains two separate numbers signifying that there are in fact two separate statement entries, one in respect of the Settlement Account and one in respect of the CHG/COM Acct. If the user wishes to see either of these he must first of all invoke STMT.ENTRY followed by the desired function and then at 'AWAITING ID' type either: 673732684.480001 where the addition of the suffix '0001' identifies the statement entry in respect of the settlement account or, 673732684.480002 where the addition of the suffix '0002' identifies the statement entry in respect of the CHG/COM ACCT. Example 3: A third example might be that of a category entry generated at initiation of a contract where commission or charges have been debited to the customer and credited to a profit and loss category code. In this case the following entries are generated on the contract: SV1 STMT.NO ............... 673732684.48 SV3 STMT.NO ............... 1 Once again the standard type number is generated and inserted at S.V.1. Now, however, S.V.2 is replaced by S.V.3 which now identifies the number in S.V.1 as a category entry and not a statement entry. To call this category entry record onto the screen the user must now type: CATEG.ENTRY at 'AWAITING APPLICATION' followed by: 673732684.480001 at 'AWAITING ID' Validation Rules: Internal multivalue field.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        List<TField> -

      • getStmtNo

        public TField getStmtNo(int idx)
        Returns the StmtNo at the specified position in this collection.

        Field description: A sub-value number generated automatically by the system which identifies either a statement entry or a category entry in respect of a contract. The system will automatically insert a number into this field and this number may refer to a statement entry or a category entry depending on the value contained in the corresponding multivalue fields. The following examples will illustrate the use of this field. Example 1: On the start date of a FRA contract there will be an entry on the Settlement Account and the following type of number will be generated at this field: SV1 STMT.NO ........... 673732684.48 SV2 STMT.NO ........... 1 The number automatically generated in S.V.1 is unique to the contract in question and is built in the following way: 1. The first four digits '6737' indicate the number of days since the 1st of January 1968. In our example, it corresponds to the 11th of June 1986. 2. The next five digits '32684' indicate the number of seconds since midnight. In our example, it corresponds to an entry generated on line at 09:04:44 AM. 3. The last two digits '48' indicate the number of hundreds of seconds. The value assigned (again automatically) to S.V.2 identifies the number in S.V.1 as a statement entry number. If the user wishes to call this statement entry record on to the screen the user will invoke the STMT.ENTRY Application and then type the following at 'AWAITING ID': 67372684.480001 where the suffix '0001' identifies it as the first statement entry (there may be more than one as the next example will illustrate). Example 2: A second example outlined here is similar to example 1 in that there is a statement entry on start date for both the Settlement Account and the CHG/COM Acct. The system handles this case as follows: SV.1 STMT.NO ........... 673732684.48 SV.2 STMT.NO ........... 1-2 Once again S.V.1 contains the identification number automatically generated by the system while S.V.2 now contains two separate numbers signifying that there are in fact two separate statement entries, one in respect of the Settlement Account and one in respect of the CHG/COM Acct. If the user wishes to see either of these he must first of all invoke STMT.ENTRY followed by the desired function and then at 'AWAITING ID' type either: 673732684.480001 where the addition of the suffix '0001' identifies the statement entry in respect of the settlement account or, 673732684.480002 where the addition of the suffix '0002' identifies the statement entry in respect of the CHG/COM ACCT. Example 3: A third example might be that of a category entry generated at initiation of a contract where commission or charges have been debited to the customer and credited to a profit and loss category code. In this case the following entries are generated on the contract: SV1 STMT.NO ............... 673732684.48 SV3 STMT.NO ............... 1 Once again the standard type number is generated and inserted at S.V.1. Now, however, S.V.2 is replaced by S.V.3 which now identifies the number in S.V.1 as a category entry and not a statement entry. To call this category entry record onto the screen the user must now type: CATEG.ENTRY at 'AWAITING APPLICATION' followed by: 673732684.480001 at 'AWAITING ID' Validation Rules: Internal multivalue field.

        Parameters:
        idx - idx of the element to return
        Returns:
        TField -

      • getTotAccrual

        public TField getTotAccrual()
        Returns the TotAccrual

        Field description: Indicates the total accrual amount in the (accrual) FRA currency. This amount will be accrued from the START.DATE to the MATURITY.DATE on a linear basis. It must be remembered that for all HEDGE contracts, the settlement amount (profit or loss) which is received or paid on the settlement date will be accrued during the notional period of the FRA contract (from START to MATURITY date) as an interest income or expense. The offset to this entry is a contra entry in the suspense account "Unearned Interest and Discount" (when profit) or "Interest Paid In Advance" (when settlement amount = loss). Validation Rules: Standard T24 amount format. System generated field when the FRA TYPE is equal to "HEDGE". This amount is always identical to the settlement amount.

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The TotAccrual

      • getUniTranId

        public TField getUniTranId()
        Returns the UniTranId

        Field description: Part of Regulatory Reporting information to a Trade Repository All Trades should have a Unique Transaction Identifier (UTI) which is generated, communicated and matched Determination of who generates the UTI should follow the existing industry best practices for that Asset class The UTI.USI.API attached in OC.PARAMETER and invoked during FRA deal capture determines who is the party responsible for UTI generation and does the following. If a value is present during deal capture the API is not invoked, on the assumption that the UTI is generated and supplied by the other Counterparty. If no value is present during the deal capture, the API is invoked to determine the party responsible for generating the UTI. If the Other counterparty is responsible, still an UTI is generated with a suffix as TEMP to show that the UTI from the other counterparty is awaited and in the meantime, the reporting is done with a Temporary ID. If T24 Bank is responsible for UTI generation, then the same is generated without TEMP. Where a reporting has been made with UTI having TEMP as suffix and subsequently the Counterparty supplies the UTI, the following procedure has to be followed to ensure reporting with actual UTI. The field Action Type needs to be changed to E and record to be authorized. Later, the UTI field should be modified with the actual UTI received. Set the Action Type field to N and authorize the record. In this way, the previous reporting gets cancelled and the new reporting goes with correct UTI. Input to this field is allowed only when OC module is installed Validation Rules : can contain up to 52 alphanumeric characters

        Parameters:
        Returns:
        TField - The UniTranId

      • getUniqueProdId

        public TField getUniqueProdId()
        Returns the UniqueProdId

        Field description: Part of Regulatory Reporting information to a Trade Repository. Denotes the unique product identifier. When a Unique Product Identifier (UPI) is available the same is mentioned here. When it UPI is not available there are other alternatives allowed like ISIN, AII, CFI. Hence no validations are created Input to this field is allowed only when OC module is installed Validation Rules: This is an OPTIONAL field

      • insertBankAddr

        public void insertBankAddr(java.lang.CharSequence param, int pos)
        Insert the specified BankAddr to the specified position in the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: Identifies the full name and address of a Beneficiary Bank, in respect of the Settlement Amount, where no Agent details are maintained for this Beneficiary Bank. This field provides flexibility during input of transactions where external movements of funds are involved. When you do not currently maintain a Customer reference for a third or fourth party bank, you can use this field to enter the full details of the name and address of the Beneficiary Bank directly. It is important to note that only one address, as free format, has been included in the module. This means that, in the case of a four party transfer, at least one of the two customers banks involved in the transfer of funds must have a Customer reference and the AGENCY defined. Once the payment has been sent, this field cannot be changed. for external delivery of Settlement Amount (Loss) -------------- -------------- | GLOBUS | | GLOBUS | | |=========>| NOSTRO | | BANK | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | | -------------- -------------- | | | -------------- May be BEN.BANK1--------->| INTERMEDIARY | or BANK.ADDR--------->| | | | OPTIONAL | | | | | BANK | | | -------------- | | | -------------- May be BEN.BANK1--------->| ACCOUNT | or BEN.BANK2--------->| WITH | or BANK.ADDR--------->| | | | | | | BANK | | | -------------- MANDATORY IF PAYMENT THRU NOSTRO and no Agency details exist. The following summarises the rules concerning the use of the 3 fields BEN.BANK1, BEN.BANK2 and BANK.ADDR: (iv) BEN.BANK1 may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank(i.e. the final destination of the funds) or an INTERMEDIARY bank which will pass the funds onto a second bank. (v) BEN.BANK2 may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank (ie. the final destination of the funds) but may NOT be an INTERMEDIARY bank. (vi) BANK.ADDR may be an ACCOUNT WITH Bank (i.e. the final destination of the funds) or it may be an INTERMEDIARY Bank which will pass the funds on to a second bank. It is only used if no customer ID is available. At contract loading, if the INTERMEDIARY Bank is identified in BEN.BANK1, then the ACCOUNT WITH Bank must be input either directly at BEN.BANK2 or within BANK.ADDR in which case the system will automatically apply it to BEN BANK2. Otherwise, when the INTERMEDIARY Bank is identified within BANK.ADDR - (and is thus automatically applied to BEN.BANK1) then the ACCOUNT WITH Bank must be identified in BEN.BANK2. Validation Rules: 1 to 4 lines of 35 Alpha-numeric characters. - Type AAA. Multi-value field. (Optional input when SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro and settlement amount is a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when the contract has been done at a loss. Input in this field is only allowed when SETTLEMENT.ACCT is a Nostro. Input in this field will not be allowed if BEN.BANK1 and BEN.BANK2 have both been entered.

        Parameters:
        param - the BankAddr to append
        pos - The position where to insert the value.
        Returns:
        nothing

      • insertConfNarrative

        public void insertConfNarrative(TField param, int pos)
        Insert the specified ConfNarrative to the specified position in the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: To specify any narrative to be included on the confirmation sent to the counterparty. If the Floating Rate Option code defined in MARKET.RATE.TEXT is OTHER, which is mapped to the tag 14F of SWIFT confirmation, this field gets defaulted with the value from the field SWIFT.CODE.WORD followed by the value from the DESCRIPTION of the MARKET.RATE.TEXT. The SWIFT.CODE.WORD defined in MARKET.RATE.TEXT table is meant for use when the floating Rate Option code is OTHER. System, therefore, defaults the same if User has not keyed in the same word manually. As per SWIFT standards, the code FROP must be used if the Floating Rate Option code is OTHER. Therefore, a validation is provided to ensure that the FROP defaulted by system is retained and not manually deleted. MARKET.RATE.TEXT record is identified using REFERENCE.RATE key on the contract. In case a record is not found, then the MARKET.RATE.TEXT record that contains the RATE.KEY value same as the REFERENCE.RATE is retrieved. When REFERENCE.RATE KEY is found in multiple records,the first record of MARKET.RATE.TEXT is considered after sorting by ID. This field is mapped to the tag 72 of the SWAP Confirmation Message. Validation Rules: Multivalue field. 35 alphanumeric characters. Input is optional and no default is applicable. Maximum 4 lines of 35 characters.

        Parameters:
        param - the ConfNarrative to append
        pos - The position where to insert the value.
        Returns:
        nothing

      • insertHedgeTransIds

        public void insertHedgeTransIds(TField param, int pos)
        Insert the specified HedgeTransIds to the specified position in the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: Specifies the contracts IDs of the Assets/Liabilities where an interest rate exposure exists. The recording of this information at the FRA contract level is relevant when the FRA transaction is done specifically to reduce this risk and as such is designated as a 'Hedge' type. In various countries, local authorities require that the bank specifically identifies the Assets/Liabilities being hedged by the FRA. Validation Rules: Any value even free text if required. Multivalue field. Up to 35 alphanumeric characters for each expanded line. Input allowed in this field only when FRA TYPE = HEDGE.

        Parameters:

      • insertOverride

        public void insertOverride(java.lang.CharSequence param, int pos)
        Insert the specified Override to the specified position in the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: Contains all the override messages which the user agreed to during input. During the validation stage of a FRA contract, the system may provide the user with a series of screen override messages to indicate an anomaly, for instance, that the interest rate varies by more thatn the variation tolerance defined in the FRA parameters table. In the event that the user confirms the Override, the full text of the actual Override Message will be stored, for reference purposes on in this multivalue field. For example, if the user inserts an 'abnormal' interest rate in the field corresponding to the interest rate then when the deal is validated a warning bell will sound and a message will appear, at the foot of the screen, which reads: 'VARIANCE OF RATE EXCEEDS PERMITTED TOLERANCE' This will draw the user's attention to the rate entered, which may be a mistake and can then be corrected, or, on the other hand, it may be correct input and so the user confirms that this rate is really intended. A second example might be in respect of a contract done with a client who has a credit line established with the bank but where the start date of the intended FRA contract goes beyond the credit line expiry date. In this case when the deal is validated a warning bell will sound and a message will appear, at the foot of the screen, which reads: 'LINE EXPIRES BEFORE TXN START DATE' Once again the user's attention is drawn to the situation and either corrected or conrimed via a positive response to the Override Message. If, subsequently, the contract record is either fully displayed or printed, then all override messages will be present. Validation Rules: Internal field. Multivalue field.

        Parameters:
        param - the Override to append
        pos - The position where to insert the value.
        Returns:
        nothing

      • insertSetlAdvSent

        public void insertSetlAdvSent(TField param, int pos)
        Insert the specified SetlAdvSent to the specified position in the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: Specifies the date and time when the settlement advice details have been passed over to the T24 Delivery module for onward communication to the receiver of the message. The FRA call to the T24 Delivery Module is acknowledged by the latter, sending back the ID it has generated for the message. This ID takes the following form: D 1986 1105 - 334335 where: D means a message is to be delivered (as opposed to R for a message received). 1986 is the current year 11 is the current month number 09 is the current day and, 334335 is a serial number taken form the computer time clock, i.e. the number of seconds (in tenths) elapsed since midnight. This number corresponds to 09:17:13 AM. Validation Rules: Content is automatically generated.

        Parameters:
        param - the SetlAdvSent to append
        pos - The position where to insert the value.
        Returns:
        nothing

      • insertStmtNo

        public void insertStmtNo(java.lang.CharSequence param, int pos)
        Insert the specified StmtNo to the specified position in the collection.
        Throws an UnsupportedOperationException if the object is not modifiable.

        Field description: A sub-value number generated automatically by the system which identifies either a statement entry or a category entry in respect of a contract. The system will automatically insert a number into this field and this number may refer to a statement entry or a category entry depending on the value contained in the corresponding multivalue fields. The following examples will illustrate the use of this field. Example 1: On the start date of a FRA contract there will be an entry on the Settlement Account and the following type of number will be generated at this field: SV1 STMT.NO ........... 673732684.48 SV2 STMT.NO ........... 1 The number automatically generated in S.V.1 is unique to the contract in question and is built in the following way: 1. The first four digits '6737' indicate the number of days since the 1st of January 1968. In our example, it corresponds to the 11th of June 1986. 2. The next five digits '32684' indicate the number of seconds since midnight. In our example, it corresponds to an entry generated on line at 09:04:44 AM. 3. The last two digits '48' indicate the number of hundreds of seconds. The value assigned (again automatically) to S.V.2 identifies the number in S.V.1 as a statement entry number. If the user wishes to call this statement entry record on to the screen the user will invoke the STMT.ENTRY Application and then type the following at 'AWAITING ID': 67372684.480001 where the suffix '0001' identifies it as the first statement entry (there may be more than one as the next example will illustrate). Example 2: A second example outlined here is similar to example 1 in that there is a statement entry on start date for both the Settlement Account and the CHG/COM Acct. The system handles this case as follows: SV.1 STMT.NO ........... 673732684.48 SV.2 STMT.NO ........... 1-2 Once again S.V.1 contains the identification number automatically generated by the system while S.V.2 now contains two separate numbers signifying that there are in fact two separate statement entries, one in respect of the Settlement Account and one in respect of the CHG/COM Acct. If the user wishes to see either of these he must first of all invoke STMT.ENTRY followed by the desired function and then at 'AWAITING ID' type either: 673732684.480001 where the addition of the suffix '0001' identifies the statement entry in respect of the settlement account or, 673732684.480002 where the addition of the suffix '0002' identifies the statement entry in respect of the CHG/COM ACCT. Example 3: A third example might be that of a category entry generated at initiation of a contract where commission or charges have been debited to the customer and credited to a profit and loss category code. In this case the following entries are generated on the contract: SV1 STMT.NO ............... 673732684.48 SV3 STMT.NO ............... 1 Once again the standard type number is generated and inserted at S.V.1. Now, however, S.V.2 is replaced by S.V.3 which now identifies the number in S.V.1 as a category entry and not a statement entry. To call this category entry record onto the screen the user must now type: CATEG.ENTRY at 'AWAITING APPLICATION' followed by: 673732684.480001 at 'AWAITING ID' Validation Rules: Internal multivalue field.

        Parameters:
        param - the StmtNo to append
        pos - The position where to insert the value.
        Returns:
        nothing
